      <p>
       <b>
        Gibraltar
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/dʒ/: 'j' in 'jam'">
            dʒ
           </span>
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'b' in 'buy'">
            b
           </span>
           <span title="'r' in 'rye'">
            r
           </span>
           <span title="/ɔː/: 'au' in 'fraud'">
            ɔː
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="'t' in 'tie'">
            t
           </span>
           <span title="/ər/: 'er' in 'letter'">
            ər
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key">
        <i title="English pronunciation respelling">
         ji-
         <span style="font-size:90%">
          BRAWL
         </span>
         -tər
        </i>
       </a>
       ,
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/dʒ/: 'j' in 'jam'">
            dʒ
           </span>
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'b' in 'buy'">
            b
           </span>
           <span title="'r' in 'rye'">
            r
           </span>
           <span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">
            ɒ
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="'t' in 'tie'">
            t
           </span>
           <span title="/ər/: 'er' in 'letter'">
            ər
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key">
        <i title="English pronunciation respelling">
         ji-
         <span style="font-size:90%">
          BROL
         </span>
         -tər
        </i>
       </a>
       or other permutations;
       <small>
        Spanish pronunciation:
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">
         [xiβɾalˈtaɾ]
        </a>
       </span>
       ) is a
       <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">
        British Overseas Territory
       </a>
       located at the southern tip of the
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">
        Iberian Peninsula
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It has an area of 6.7 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (2.6 sq mi) and is
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar%E2%80%93Spain_border" title="Gibraltar–Spain border">
        bordered to the north
       </a>
       by Spain. The landscape is dominated by the
       <a href="/wiki/Rock_of_Gibraltar" title="Rock of Gibraltar">
        Rock of Gibraltar
       </a>
       at the foot of which is a densely populated city area, home to over 30,000 people, primarily
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gibraltarian_people" title="Gibraltarian people">
        Gibraltarians
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       An Anglo-Dutch force
       <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Gibraltar" title="Capture of Gibraltar">
        captured Gibraltar
       </a>
       from
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       in 1704 during the
       <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">
        War of the Spanish Succession
       </a>
       on behalf of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburg" title="Habsburg">
        Habsburg
       </a>
       claim to the Spanish throne. The territory was subsequently ceded to
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">
        Great Britain
       </a>
       "in perpetuity" under the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" title="Treaty of Utrecht">
        Treaty of Utrecht
       </a>
       in 1713. During World War II it was an important base for the
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">
        Royal Navy
       </a>
       as it controlled the entrance and exit to the
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">
        Mediterranean Sea
       </a>
       , which is only eight miles (13 km) wide at this naval "
       <a href="/wiki/Choke_point" title="Choke point">
        choke point
       </a>
       ". It remains strategically important to this day, with half the world's seaborne trade passing through the strait.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Today Gibraltar's economy is based largely on tourism, online gambling, financial services, and cargo ship refuelling services.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maec_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Maec-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Much of it depends on access to the EU single market, which a prospective
       <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">
        Brexit
       </a>
       makes
       <a href="/wiki/Effect_of_Brexit_on_Gibraltar" title="Effect of Brexit on Gibraltar">
        uncertain
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The sovereignty of Gibraltar is a major point of contention in
       <a href="/wiki/Spain%E2%80%93United_Kingdom_relations" title="Spain–United Kingdom relations">
        Anglo-Spanish relations
       </a>
       as Spain asserts
       <a href="/wiki/Disputed_status_of_Gibraltar" title="Disputed status of Gibraltar">
        a claim to the territory
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maec_15-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Maec-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Gibraltarians overwhelmingly rejected proposals for Spanish sovereignty in a
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_sovereignty_referendum,_1967" title="Gibraltar sovereignty referendum, 1967">
        1967 referendum
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_sovereignty_referendum,_2002" title="Gibraltar sovereignty referendum, 2002">
        again in 2002
       </a>
       . Under the
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Constitution_Order_2006" title="Gibraltar Constitution Order 2006">
        Gibraltar constitution of 2006
       </a>
       , Gibraltar governs its own affairs, though some powers, such as defence and foreign relations, remain the responsibility of the
       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom">
        British government
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Name">
        Name
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The name
       <i>
        Gibraltar
       </i>
       is the Spanish derivation of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
        Arabic
       </a>
       name
       <i>
        Jabal Ṭāriq
       </i>
       (
       <span lang="ar">
        جبل طارق
       </span>
       ), meaning "Mountain of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tariq_ibn-Ziyad" title="Tariq ibn-Ziyad">
        Tariq
       </a>
       ". It refers to the
       <a href="/wiki/Rock_of_Gibraltar" title="Rock of Gibraltar">
        Rock of Gibraltar
       </a>
       , which was named after the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Umayyad" title="Umayyad">
        Umayyad
       </a>
       general
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tariq_ibn-Ziyad" title="Tariq ibn-Ziyad">
        Tariq ibn-Ziyad
       </a>
       who led the initial incursion
       <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_conquest_of_Hispania" title="Umayyad conquest of Hispania">
        into Iberia in advance of the main Umayyad force
       </a>
       in 711 under the command of Umayyad Caliph
       <a href="/wiki/Al-Walid_I" title="Al-Walid I">
        Al-Walid I
       </a>
       . Earlier, it was known as
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mons_Calpe" title="Mons Calpe">
         Mons Calpe
        </a>
       </i>
       , a name of Phoenician origin and one of the
       <a href="/wiki/Pillars_of_Hercules" title="Pillars of Hercules">
        Pillars of Hercules
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hills-13_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hills-13-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">
        Early history
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Gibraltar" title="History of Gibraltar">
        History of Gibraltar
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Moorish_Castle.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="2136" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_Moorish_Castle.jpg/170px-The_Moorish_Castle.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_Moorish_Castle.jpg/255px-The_Moorish_Castle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_Moorish_Castle.jpg/340px-The_Moorish_Castle.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Moorish_Castle.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         View of the northern face of the
         <a href="/wiki/Moorish_Castle" title="Moorish Castle">
          Moorish Castle
         </a>
         's Tower of Homage. Built in the 14th century.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Evidence of
       <a href="/wiki/Neanderthal" title="Neanderthal">
        Neanderthal
       </a>
       habitation in Gibraltar has been discovered at
       <a href="/wiki/Gorham%27s_Cave" title="Gorham's Cave">
        Gorham's Cave
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Within recorded history, the first inhabitants were the
       <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">
        Phoenicians
       </a>
       , around 950 BC. Subsequently, Gibraltar became known as one of the
       <a href="/wiki/Pillars_of_Hercules" title="Pillars of Hercules">
        Pillars of Hercules
       </a>
       , after the
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">
        Greek
       </a>
       legend of the creation of the
       <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">
        Strait of Gibraltar
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Heracles" title="Heracles">
        Heracles
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Carthage" title="Carthage">
        Carthaginians
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">
        Romans
       </a>
       also established semi-permanent settlements. After the collapse of the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman Empire
       </a>
       , Gibraltar came briefly under the control of the
       <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">
        Vandals
       </a>
       , who crossed into Africa at the invitation of
       <a href="/wiki/Bonifacius" title="Bonifacius">
        Boniface
       </a>
       , the Count (or commander) of the territory.
      </p>
      <p>
       The area later formed part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">
        Visigothic Kingdom
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">
        Hispania
       </a>
       from 414 AD until the
       <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_conquest_of_Hispania" title="Umayyad conquest of Hispania">
        Islamic conquest of Iberia
       </a>
       in 711 AD.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Settlement">
        Settlement
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Settlement">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 1160, the
       <a href="/wiki/Almohad_Caliphate" title="Almohad Caliphate">
        Almohad
       </a>
       Sultan
       <a href="/wiki/Abd_al-Mu%27min" title="Abd al-Mu'min">
        Abd al-Mu'min
       </a>
       ordered that a permanent settlement, including a castle, be built. It received the name of Medinat al-Fath (City of the Victory).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-norris_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-norris-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On completion of the works in the town, the Sultan crossed the Strait to look at the works and stayed in Gibraltar for two months. The Tower of Homage of the
       <a href="/wiki/Moorish_Castle" title="Moorish Castle">
        Moorish Castle
       </a>
       remains standing today. From 1274 onwards, the town was fought over and captured by the
       <a href="/wiki/Nasrid_dynasty" title="Nasrid dynasty">
        Nasrids
       </a>
       of Granada (in 1237 and 1374), the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marinids" title="Marinids">
        Marinids
       </a>
       of Morocco (in 1274 and 1333) and the kings of
       <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">
        Castile
       </a>
       (in 1309). In 1462, Gibraltar was finally captured by
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Alonso_de_Guzm%C3%A1n,_1st_Duke_of_Medina_Sidonia" title="Juan Alonso de Guzmán, 1st Duke of Medina Sidonia">
        Juan Alonso de Guzmán, 1st Duke of Medina Sidonia
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After the conquest, King
       <a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_Castile" title="Henry IV of Castile">
        Henry IV of Castile
       </a>
       assumed the additional title of
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Gibraltar" title="Kingdom of Gibraltar">
        King of Gibraltar
       </a>
       , establishing it as part of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Comarca" title="Comarca">
         comarca
        </a>
       </i>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Campo_de_Gibraltar" title="Campo de Gibraltar">
        Campo Llano de Gibraltar
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Six years later, Gibraltar was restored to the Duke of Medina Sidonia, who sold it in 1474 to a group of 4350
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Converso" title="Converso">
         conversos
        </a>
       </i>
       (Christian converts from Judaism) from
       <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Spain" title="Córdoba, Spain">
        Cordova
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seville,_Spain" title="Seville, Spain">
        Seville
       </a>
       and in exchange for maintaining the garrison of the town for two years, after which time they were expelled, returning to their home towns or moving on to other parts of Spain.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1501, Gibraltar passed back to the Spanish Crown, and
       <a href="/wiki/Isabella_I_of_Castile" title="Isabella I of Castile">
        Isabella I of Castile
       </a>
       issued a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_warrant_(document)" title="Royal warrant (document)">
        Royal Warrant
       </a>
       granting Gibraltar the coat of arms that it still uses today.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1704, during the
       <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">
        War of the Spanish Succession
       </a>
       , a combined
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">
        Anglo
       </a>
       -
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">
        Dutch
       </a>
       fleet, representing the
       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Alliance_(League_of_Augsburg)" title="Grand Alliance (League of Augsburg)">
        Grand Alliance
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Gibraltar" title="Capture of Gibraltar">
        captured the town of Gibraltar
       </a>
       on behalf of the
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_VI,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles VI, Holy Roman Emperor">
        Archduke Charles of Austria
       </a>
       in his campaign to become King of Spain. The occupation of the town by Alliance forces caused the exodus of the population to the surrounding area of the Campo de Gibraltar.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As the Alliance's campaign faltered, the 1713
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" title="Treaty of Utrecht">
        Treaty of Utrecht
       </a>
       was negotiated and ceded control of Gibraltar to Britain to secure Britain's withdrawal from the war. Unsuccessful attempts by Spanish monarchs to regain Gibraltar were made with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siege_of_Gibraltar_(1727)" title="Siege of Gibraltar (1727)">
        siege of 1727
       </a>
       and again with the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Siege_of_Gibraltar" title="Great Siege of Gibraltar">
        Great Siege of Gibraltar
       </a>
       (1779 to 1783), during the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_War_of_Independence" title="American War of Independence">
        American War of Independence
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Gibraltar became a key base for the
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">
        Royal Navy
       </a>
       and played an important role prior to the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trafalgar" title="Battle of Trafalgar">
        Battle of Trafalgar
       </a>
       (21 October 1805) and during the
       <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">
        Crimean War
       </a>
       of 1854–56, because of its strategic location. Its strategic value increased with the opening of the
       <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">
        Suez Canal
       </a>
       , as it lay on the sea route between the UK and the British Empire east of Suez. In the later 19th century, there were major investments in improving the fortifications and the port.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG/250px-Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG/375px-Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG/500px-Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Buildings of the former
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HM_Dockyard,_Gibraltar" title="HM Dockyard, Gibraltar">
          HM Dockyard, Gibraltar
         </a>
         , dating from the 1895 expansion
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_history">
        Modern history
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Modern history">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar,_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2480" data-file-width="2486" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar%2C_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg/220px-Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar%2C_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar%2C_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg/330px-Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar%2C_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar%2C_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg/440px-Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar%2C_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar,_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         During the Second World War, a
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Douglas_Dakota" title="Douglas Dakota">
          Douglas Dakota
         </a>
         of
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BOAC" title="BOAC">
          BOAC
         </a>
         is silhouetted at Gibraltar by the batteries of searchlights on the Rock, as crews prepare it for a night flight to the United Kingdom.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the
       <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Gibraltar_during_World_War_II" title="Military history of Gibraltar during World War II">
        Second World War
       </a>
       , Gibraltar's civilian population was evacuated (mainly to London, but also to parts of
       <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
        Morocco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">
        Madeira
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">
        Jamaica
       </a>
       ) and the Rock was strengthened as a
       <a href="/wiki/Fortification" title="Fortification">
        fortress
       </a>
       . The naval base and the ships based there played a key role in the provisioning and supply of the island of
       <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">
        Malta
       </a>
       during
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Malta_(World_War_II)" title="Siege of Malta (World War II)">
        its long siege
       </a>
       . As well as frequent short runs (known as 'Club Runs') towards
       <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">
        Malta
       </a>
       to fly off aircraft reinforcements (initially
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hawker_hurricane" title="Hawker hurricane">
        Hurricanes
       </a>
       but later, notably from the USN aircraft carrier
       <a href="/wiki/USS_Wasp_(CV-7)" title="USS Wasp (CV-7)">
        Wasp
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Supermarine_Spitfire" title="Supermarine Spitfire">
        Spitfires
       </a>
       ), the critical
       <a href="/wiki/Operation_Pedestal" title="Operation Pedestal">
        Operation Pedestal
       </a>
       convoy was run from Gibraltar in August 1942. This resupplied the island at a critical time in the face of concentrated air attacks from German and Italian forces. Spanish dictator
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">
        Francisco Franco
       </a>
       's reluctance to allow the
       <a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">
        German Army
       </a>
       onto Spanish soil frustrated a German plan to capture the Rock, codenamed
       <a href="/wiki/Operation_Felix" title="Operation Felix">
        Operation Felix
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 1950s, Franco renewed Spain's claim to sovereignty over Gibraltar and restricted movement between Gibraltar and Spain. Gibraltarians voted overwhelmingly to remain under British sovereignty in the
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_sovereignty_referendum,_1967" title="Gibraltar sovereignty referendum, 1967">
        Gibraltar sovereignty referendum, 1967
       </a>
       , which led to the passing of the
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Constitution_Order_1969" title="Gibraltar Constitution Order 1969">
        Gibraltar Constitution Order
       </a>
       in 1969. In response, Spain completely closed the border with Gibraltar and severed all communication links.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The border with Spain was partially reopened in 1982 and fully reopened in 1985 before Spain's accession to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Community" title="European Community">
        European Community
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_sovereignty_referendum,_2002" title="Gibraltar sovereignty referendum, 2002">
        a referendum held in 2002
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gibraltarian_people" title="Gibraltarian people">
        Gibraltarians
       </a>
       rejected by an overwhelming majority (98%) a proposal of shared sovereignty on which
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
        Britain
       </a>
       were said to have reached "broad agreement".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The British government has committed itself to respecting the Gibraltarians' wishes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Constitution_Order_2006" title="Gibraltar Constitution Order 2006">
        new Constitution Order
       </a>
       was approved in referendum in 2006. A process of tripartite negotiations started in 2006 between Spain, Gibraltar and the UK, ending some restrictions and dealing with disputes in some specific areas such as air movements, customs procedures, telecommunications, pensions and cultural exchange.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_referendum_on_membership_of_the_European_Union" title="British referendum on membership of the European Union">
        British referendum on membership of the European Union
       </a>
       96% of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gibraltarians_voted_to_remain" title="Gibraltarians voted to remain">
        Gibraltarians voted to remain
       </a>
       on an 82% turnout.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Spain renewed calls for joint Spanish–British control of the peninsula,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which were strongly rebuffed by Gibraltar's Chief Minister.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">
        Governance
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Governance">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Gibraltar" title="Politics of Gibraltar">
        Politics of Gibraltar
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Disputed_status_of_Gibraltar" title="Disputed status of Gibraltar">
        Disputed status of Gibraltar
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Political_development_in_modern_Gibraltar" title="Political development in modern Gibraltar">
        Political development in modern Gibraltar
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="4752" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg/220px-The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg/330px-The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg/440px-The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Main Street entrance to the Governor's Residence,
         <a href="/wiki/The_Convent_(Gibraltar)" title="The Convent (Gibraltar)">
          The Convent
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg/220px-Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg/330px-Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg/440px-Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/John_Mackintosh_Square" title="John Mackintosh Square">
          John Mackintosh Square
         </a>
         entrance to the
         <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Parliament" title="Gibraltar Parliament">
          Gibraltar Parliament
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Under its current
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Constitution_Order_2006" title="Gibraltar Constitution Order 2006">
        constitution
       </a>
       , Gibraltar has almost complete internal
       <a href="/wiki/Self-governance" title="Self-governance">
        self-governance
       </a>
       through a
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Parliament" title="Gibraltar Parliament">
        parliament
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-publications.parliament.uk_34-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-publications.parliament.uk-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       elected for a term of up to four years. The
       <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">
        unicameral
       </a>
       parliament presently consists of 17 elected members, and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Speakers_of_the_Gibraltar_Parliament" title="List of Speakers of the Gibraltar Parliament">
        Speaker
       </a>
       who is not elected, but appointed by a resolution of the parliament.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Gibraltar" title="Government of Gibraltar">
        government
       </a>
       consists of 10 elected members. The head of state is the British monarch, currently
       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">
        Queen Elizabeth II
       </a>
       , who is represented by the
       <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Gibraltar" title="Governor of Gibraltar">
        Governor of Gibraltar
       </a>
       . The governor enacts day-to-day matters on the advice of the Gibraltar Parliament, but is responsible to the British government in respect of defence, foreign policy, internal security and general good governance. Judicial and other appointments are made on behalf of the monarch in consultation with the
       <a href="/wiki/Chief_Minister_of_Gibraltar" title="Chief Minister of Gibraltar">
        head of the elected government
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_general_election,_2011" title="Gibraltar general election, 2011">
        2011 election
       </a>
       was contested by the
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Social_Democrats" title="Gibraltar Social Democrats">
        Gibraltar Social Democrats
       </a>
       (GSD),
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Socialist_Labour_Party" title="Gibraltar Socialist Labour Party">
        Gibraltar Socialist Labour Party
       </a>
       (GSLP)-
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Liberal_Party" title="Gibraltar Liberal Party">
        Gibraltar Liberal Party
       </a>
       (GLP) Alliance and the
       <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Democratic_Party_(Gibraltar)" title="Progressive Democratic Party (Gibraltar)">
        Progressive Democratic Party
       </a>
       (PDP). The PDP is a new party, formed in 2006 and fielded candidates in the 2007 election, but none were elected. The head of government is the
       <a href="/wiki/Chief_Minister_of_Gibraltar" title="Chief Minister of Gibraltar">
        Chief Minister
       </a>
       (as of December 2011,
       <a href="/wiki/Fabian_Picardo" title="Fabian Picardo">
        Fabian Picardo
       </a>
       ). All local political parties oppose any transfer of sovereignty to Spain, instead supporting
       <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">
        self-determination
       </a>
       . The main UK opposition parties also support this policy, and it is British government policy not to engage in talks about the sovereignty of Gibraltar without the consent of the people of Gibraltar.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Gibraltar is part of the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       , having joined through the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Communities_Act_1972_(UK)" title="European Communities Act 1972 (UK)">
        European Communities Act 1972 (UK)
       </a>
       , which gave effect to the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Accession_1972" title="Treaty of Accession 1972">
        Treaty of Accession 1972
       </a>
       , as a dependent territory of the United Kingdom under what was then article 227(4) of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_Establishing_the_European_Community" title="Treaty Establishing the European Community">
        Treaty Establishing the European Community
       </a>
       covering
       <a href="/wiki/Special_member_state_territories_and_the_European_Union#Gibraltar" title="Special member state territories and the European Union">
        special member state territories
       </a>
       , with exemption from some areas such as the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union" title="European Union Customs Union">
        European Union Customs Union
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">
        Common Agricultural Policy
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">
        Schengen Area
       </a>
       . It is the only
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territory" title="British Overseas Territory">
        British Overseas Territory
       </a>
       which is part of the European Union. After a 10-year campaign for the right to vote in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elections_in_the_European_Union" title="Elections in the European Union">
        European elections
       </a>
       , since 2004 the people of Gibraltar have participated in elections for the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">
        European Parliament
       </a>
       as part of the
       <a href="/wiki/South_West_England_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="South West England (European Parliament constituency)">
        South West England constituency
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 23 June 2016 Gibraltar voted along with the United Kingdom in the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">
        EU referendum
       </a>
       ; 96% of its population voted to remain, but the overall United Kingdom result gave a 51.9% majority to leaving the EU.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Gibraltar was nominated to be included on the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_Non-Self-Governing_Territories" title="United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories">
        United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories
       </a>
       by the United Kingdom when the list was created in 1946
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and has been listed ever since.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The government of Gibraltar has actively worked to have Gibraltar removed from the list,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and in 2008 the British government declared Gibraltar's continued presence on the list an anachronism.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Gibraltar is not a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">
        Commonwealth of Nations
       </a>
       but was granted Associate Membership of the
       <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Foundation" title="Commonwealth Foundation">
        Commonwealth Foundation
       </a>
       in 2004. Gibraltar has competed in the
       <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">
        Commonwealth Games
       </a>
       since 1958.
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">

       </span>

         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">

       <a href="/wiki/Rock_of_Gibraltar" title="Rock of Gibraltar">
        Rock of Gibraltar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Gibraltar" title="Bay of Gibraltar">
        Bay of Gibraltar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">
        Strait of Gibraltar
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Artificial_Reef" title="Gibraltar Artificial Reef">
        Gibraltar Artificial Reef
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg/220px-Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg/330px-Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg/440px-Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         View of the Rock of Gibraltar from the
         <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Steps" title="Mediterranean Steps">
          Mediterranean Steps
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_aerial_view_looking_northwest.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="819" data-file-width="1024" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Gibraltar_aerial_view_looking_northwest.jpg/220px-Gibraltar_aerial_view_looking_northwest.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Gibraltar_aerial_view_looking_northwest.jpg/330px-Gibraltar_aerial_view_looking_northwest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Gibraltar_aerial_view_looking_northwest.jpg/440px-Gibraltar_aerial_view_looking_northwest.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_aerial_view_looking_northwest.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Gibraltar from the air, looking north-west
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Gibraltar's territory covers 6.7 square kilometres (2.6 sq mi) and shares a 1.2-kilometre (0.75 mi) land border with Spain. The town of
       <a href="/wiki/La_L%C3%ADnea_de_la_Concepci%C3%B3n" title="La Línea de la Concepción">
        La Línea de la Concepción
       </a>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_C%C3%A1diz" title="List of municipalities in Cádiz">
        municipality
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_C%C3%A1diz" title="Province of Cádiz">
        province of Cádiz
       </a>
       , lies on the Spanish side of the border. The Spanish hinterland forms the
       <a href="/wiki/Comarca" title="Comarca">
        comarca
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Campo_de_Gibraltar" title="Campo de Gibraltar">
        Campo de Gibraltar
       </a>
       (literally "Countryside of Gibraltar"). The shoreline measures 12 kilometres (7.5 mi) in length. There are two coasts ("Sides") of Gibraltar: the East Side, which contains the settlements of
       <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Bay,_Gibraltar" title="Sandy Bay, Gibraltar">
        Sandy Bay
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_Bay" title="Catalan Bay">
        Catalan Bay
       </a>
       ; and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Westside_(Gibraltar)" title="Westside (Gibraltar)">
        Westside
       </a>
       , where the vast majority of the population lives. Gibraltar has no administrative divisions but is divided into seven
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Major_Residential_Areas" title="Gibraltar Major Residential Areas">
        Major Residential Areas
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Having negligible
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">
        natural resources
       </a>
       and few natural
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freshwater" title="Freshwater">
        freshwater
       </a>
       resources, limited to natural wells in the north, until recently Gibraltar used large concrete and/or natural rock
       <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">
        water catchments
       </a>
       to collect rainwater. Fresh water from the boreholes is supplemented by two
       <a href="/wiki/Desalination" title="Desalination">
        desalination
       </a>
       plants: a
       <a href="/wiki/Reverse_osmosis" title="Reverse osmosis">
        reverse osmosis
       </a>
       plant, constructed in a tunnel within the rock, and a
       <a href="/wiki/Multi-stage_flash_distillation" title="Multi-stage flash distillation">
        multi-stage flash distillation
       </a>
       plant at North Mole.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Gibraltar's terrain consists of the 426-metre-high (1,398 ft)
       <a href="/wiki/Rock_of_Gibraltar" title="Rock of Gibraltar">
        Rock of Gibraltar
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       made of
       <a href="/wiki/Jurassic" title="Jurassic">
        Jurassic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">
        limestone
       </a>
       , and the narrow coastal lowland surrounding it. It contains many tunnelled roads, most of which are still operated by the military and closed to the general public.
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Gibraltar" title="Climate of Gibraltar">
        Climate of Gibraltar
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Gibraltar has a
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">
        Mediterranean climate
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
        Köppen climate classification
       </a>
       <i>
        Csa
       </i>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with mild, rainy winters and warm, dry summers. As is the case for nearby
       <a href="/wiki/Algeciras" title="Algeciras">
        Algeciras
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tarifa" title="Tarifa">
        Tarifa
       </a>
       , summers are significantly cooler and annual temperature more constant than other cities on the southern coast of the Iberian peninsula because of its position on the Strait of Gibraltar. Rain occurs mainly in winter, with summer being generally dry. Its average annual temperature is about 22 °C (72 °F) as a daily high and 15 °C (59 °F) as the overnight low. In the coldest month, January, the high temperature averages 16.3 °C (61.3 °F) and the overnight low is 11 °C (52 °F) and the average sea temperature is 16 °C (61 °F). In the warmest month, August, the daily hight temperature is 25 °C (77 °F), the overnight low is 20 °C (68 °F), and the average sea temperature is 22 °C (72 °F).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DWD_52-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-DWD-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weather2travel_53-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-weather2travel-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

        </td>
