      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">
        Flora and fauna
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Gibraltar" title="List of mammals of Gibraltar">
        List of mammals of Gibraltar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Gibraltar" title="List of birds of Gibraltar">
        List of birds of Gibraltar
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_amphibians_and_reptiles_of_Gibraltar" title="List of amphibians and reptiles of Gibraltar">
        List of amphibians and reptiles of Gibraltar
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1088" data-file-width="1632" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG/220px-Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG/330px-Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG/440px-Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Iberis_gibraltarica" title="Iberis gibraltarica">
          Gibraltar candytuft
         </a>
         growing at the
         <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Botanic_Gardens" title="Gibraltar Botanic Gardens">
          Gibraltar Botanic Gardens
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="434" data-file-width="789" height="121" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png/220px-Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png/330px-Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png/440px-Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A
         <a href="/wiki/Common_dolphin" title="Common dolphin">
          common dolphin
         </a>
         in the
         <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Gibraltar" title="Bay of Gibraltar">
          Bay of Gibraltar
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Over 500 different species of
       <a href="/wiki/Flowering_plant" title="Flowering plant">
        flowering plants
       </a>
       grow on the Rock. Gibraltar is the only place in Europe where the
       <i>
        Gibraltar candytuft
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Iberis_gibraltarica" title="Iberis gibraltarica">
         Iberis gibraltarica
        </a>
       </i>
       ) is found growing in the wild; the plant is otherwise native to North Africa. It is the symbol of the
       <a href="/wiki/Rock_of_Gibraltar#Upper_Rock_Nature_Reserve" title="Rock of Gibraltar">
        Upper Rock nature reserve
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">
        Olive
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Pine" title="Pine">
        pine
       </a>
       trees are among the most common of those growing around the Rock.
      </p>
      <p>
       Most of the Rock's upper area is covered by a
       <a href="/wiki/Nature_reserve" title="Nature reserve">
        nature reserve
       </a>
       which is home to around 230
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Barbary_macaques" title="Gibraltar Barbary macaques">
        Barbary macaques
       </a>
       , the famous "apes" of Gibraltar, which are actually
       <a href="/wiki/Monkey" title="Monkey">
        monkeys
       </a>
       . These are the only wild apes or monkeys found in Europe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This species, known scientifically as
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macaca_sylvanus" title="Macaca sylvanus">
         Macaca sylvanus
        </a>
       </i>
       , is listed as endangered by the
       <a href="/wiki/IUCN_Red_List" title="IUCN Red List">
        IUCN Red List
       </a>
       and is declining. Three-quarters of the world population live in the
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Atlas" title="Middle Atlas">
        Middle Atlas
       </a>
       mountains of
       <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
        Morocco
       </a>
       . Recent genetic studies and historical documents point to their presence on the Rock before its
       <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Gibraltar" title="Capture of Gibraltar">
        capture by the British
       </a>
       , having possibly been introduced during the Islamic period. A superstition analogous to that of the
       <a href="/wiki/Raven" title="Raven">
        ravens
       </a>
       at the
       <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_London" title="Tower of London">
        Tower of London
       </a>
       states that if the apes ever leave, so will the British. In 1944,
       <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">
        British Prime Minister
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">
        Winston Churchill
       </a>
       , was so concerned about the dwindling population of apes that he sent a message to the
       <a href="/wiki/Chief_Secretary_(British_Empire)" title="Chief Secretary (British Empire)">
        Colonial Secretary
       </a>
       requesting that something be done about the situation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Other mammals found in Gibraltar include rabbits, foxes and bats. Dolphins and whales are frequently seen in the
       <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Gibraltar" title="Bay of Gibraltar">
        Bay of Gibraltar
       </a>
       . Migrating birds are very common and Gibraltar is home to the only
       <a href="/wiki/Barbary_partridge" title="Barbary partridge">
        Barbary partridges
       </a>
       found on the European continent.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1991, Graham Watson, Gibraltar's
       <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">
        MEP
       </a>
       , highlighted
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conservationism" title="Conservationism">
        conservationists
       </a>
       ' fears that
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urban_development" title="Urban development">
        urban development
       </a>
       , tourism and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Invasive_plant_species" title="Invasive plant species">
        invasive plant species
       </a>
       were threatening Gibraltar's own plants as well as birds and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bat_species" title="Bat species">
        bat species
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">
        Environment
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Environment">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In May 2016 a report by the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">
        World Health Organization
       </a>
       showed that Gibraltar had the worst air quality in any British territory. The report concentrated on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PM10" title="PM10">
        PM10
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PM2.5" title="PM2.5">
        PM2.5
       </a>
       pollutants in the air.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Gibraltar" title="Economy of Gibraltar">
        Economy of Gibraltar
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="998" data-file-width="666" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg/170px-Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg/255px-Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg/340px-Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The semi-wild
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Barbary_macaques" title="Gibraltar Barbary macaques">
          Barbary macaques
         </a>
         are an integral feature in
         <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Gibraltar" title="Tourism in Gibraltar">
          Gibraltar's tourism
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">
        British military
       </a>
       traditionally dominated
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Gibraltar" title="Economy of Gibraltar">
        Gibraltar's economy
       </a>
       , with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naval_dockyard" title="Naval dockyard">
        naval dockyard
       </a>
       providing the bulk of economic activity. This, however, has diminished over the last 20 years, and is estimated to account for only 7 percent of the local economy, compared to over 60 percent in 1984. Today, Gibraltar's economy is dominated by four main sectors:
       <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">
        financial services
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Online_gambling" title="Online gambling">
        online gambling
       </a>
       , shipping, and tourism, which includes duty-free retail sales to visitors.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The territory also has a small manufacturing sector, with one company supplying ambulances produced from converted
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SUV" title="SUV">
        SUV
       </a>
       vehicles to the United Nations and other agencies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the early 2000s, many
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bookmaker" title="Bookmaker">
        bookmakers
       </a>
       and online gaming operators moved to Gibraltar to benefit from operating in a regulated jurisdiction with a favourable
       <a href="/wiki/Corporate_tax" title="Corporate tax">
        corporate tax
       </a>
       regime. This corporate tax regime for non-resident controlled companies was phased out by January 2011 and replaced by a still favourable fixed corporate tax rate of 10 percent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Tourism is also a significant industry. Gibraltar is a popular port for cruise ships and attracts day visitors from resorts in Spain. The Rock is a popular tourist attraction, particularly among British tourists and residents in the southern coast of Spain. It is also a popular shopping destination, and all goods and services are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Value_added_tax" title="Value added tax">
        VAT
       </a>
       free, but may be subject to Gibraltar taxes. Many of the large British high street chains have branches or franchises in Gibraltar including
       <a href="/wiki/Morrisons" title="Morrisons">
        Morrisons
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Marks_%26_Spencer" title="Marks &amp; Spencer">
        Marks &amp; Spencer
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mothercare" title="Mothercare">
        Mothercare
       </a>
       . Branches and franchises of international retailers such as
       <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Hilfiger" title="Tommy Hilfiger">
        Tommy Hilfiger
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunglass_Hut_International" title="Sunglass Hut International">
        Sunglass Hut
       </a>
       are also present in Gibraltar, as is the Spanish clothing company
       <a href="/wiki/Mango_(clothing)" title="Mango (clothing)">
        Mango
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg/220px-Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg/330px-Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg/440px-Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Queensway Quay Marina, along with
         <a href="/wiki/Ocean_Village,_Gibraltar" title="Ocean Village, Gibraltar">
          Ocean Village
         </a>
         , are two exclusive residential districts
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       A number of
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_banks_in_Gibraltar" title="List of banks in Gibraltar">
        British and international banks
       </a>
       have operations based in Gibraltar.
       <a href="/wiki/Jyske_Bank" title="Jyske Bank">
        Jyske Bank
       </a>
       claims to be the oldest bank in the country, based on Jyske's acquisition in 1987 of
       <a href="/wiki/Banco_Galliano" title="Banco Galliano">
        Banco Galliano
       </a>
       , which began operations in Gibraltar in 1855. An ancestor of
       <a href="/wiki/Barclays" title="Barclays">
        Barclays
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Egyptian_Bank" title="Anglo-Egyptian Bank">
        Anglo-Egyptian Bank
       </a>
       , entered in 1888, and Credit Foncier (now
       <a href="/wiki/Cr%C3%A9dit_Agricole" title="Crédit Agricole">
        Crédit Agricole
       </a>
       ) entered in 1920.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1967, Gibraltar enacted the Companies (Taxation and Concessions) Ordinance (now an Act), which provided for special tax treatment for international business.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This was one of the factors leading to the growth of professional services such as
       <a href="/wiki/Private_banking" title="Private banking">
        private banking
       </a>
       and captive insurance management. Gibraltar has several positive attributes as a
       <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">
        financial centre
       </a>
       , including a
       <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">
        common law
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Gibraltar" title="Law of Gibraltar">
        legal system
       </a>
       and access to the EU single market in financial services. The Financial Services Commission (FSC),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which was established by an ordinance in 1989 (now an Act) that took effect in 1991, regulates the finance sector.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1997, the Department of Trade and Industry established its Gibraltar Finance Centre (GFC) Division to facilitate the development the
       <a href="/wiki/Financial_sector_development" title="Financial sector development">
        financial sector development
       </a>
       . As of 2012
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , Gibraltar has 0.103
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Four_(audit_firms)" title="Big Four (audit firms)">
        Big Four
       </a>
       accounting firm offices per 1,000 population, the second highest in the world after the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">
        British Virgin Islands
       </a>
       , and 0.6 banks per 1,000 people, the fifth most banks per capita in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of 2017, there is
       <a href="/wiki/Effect_of_Brexit_on_Gibraltar" title="Effect of Brexit on Gibraltar">
        very significant uncertainty
       </a>
       on continuing access to the EU single market after a prospective
       <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">
        Brexit
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The currency of Gibraltar is the
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_pound" title="Gibraltar pound">
        Gibraltar pound
       </a>
       , issued by the
       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Gibraltar" title="Government of Gibraltar">
        Government of Gibraltar
       </a>
       under the terms of the 1934
       <i>
        Currency Notes Act
       </i>
       . These banknotes are
       <a href="/wiki/Legal_tender" title="Legal tender">
        legal tender
       </a>
       in Gibraltar alongside Bank of England banknotes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-currnotesact_70-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-currnotesact-70">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In a
       <a href="/wiki/Currency_board" title="Currency board">
        currency board
       </a>
       arrangement, these notes are issued against reserves of
       <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">
        sterling
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-currnotesact_70-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-currnotesact-70">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Clearing and settlement of funds is conducted in sterling.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coins_of_the_Gibraltar_pound" title="Coins of the Gibraltar pound">
        Coins
       </a>
       in circulation follow British denominations but have separate designs. Unofficially, most retail outlets in Gibraltar accept the
       <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">
        euro
       </a>
       , though some payphones and the
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Gibraltar_Post_Office" title="Royal Gibraltar Post Office">
        Royal Gibraltar Post Office
       </a>
       , along with all other government offices, do not.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Demographics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Gibraltar" title="Demographics of Gibraltar">
        Demographics of Gibraltar
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="467" data-file-width="700" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg/220px-Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg/330px-Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg/440px-Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Roman Catholic
         <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned" title="Cathedral of St. Mary the Crowned">
          Cathedral of St. Mary the Crowned
         </a>
         was built in 1462 and is the territory's oldest Catholic church.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2904" data-file-width="4352" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG/220px-Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG/330px-Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG/440px-Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple" title="Gibraltar Hindu Temple">
          Gibraltar Hindu Temple
         </a>
         , opened in 2000
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1440" data-file-width="1920" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg/220px-Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg/330px-Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg/440px-Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim-al-Ibrahim_Mosque" title="Ibrahim-al-Ibrahim Mosque">
          Ibrahim-al-Ibrahim Mosque
         </a>
         was a gift from
         <a href="/wiki/Fahd_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Fahd of Saudi Arabia">
          King Fahd
         </a>
         of
         <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">
          Saudi Arabia
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Gibraltar is one of the most densely populated territories in the world, with a usually-resident population in 2012 of 32,194
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       equivalent to approximately 4,959 inhabitants per square kilometre (12,840/sq mi). The growing demand for space is being increasingly met by
       <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">
        land reclamation
       </a>
       ; reclaimed land currently comprises approximately one tenth of the territory's total area.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">
        Ethnic groups
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gibraltarian_people" title="Gibraltarian people">
        Gibraltarian people
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The demographics of Gibraltar reflect the many
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_ethnic_groups" title="European ethnic groups">
        European
       </a>
       and other
       <a href="/wiki/Economic_migrant" title="Economic migrant">
        economic migrants
       </a>
       who came to the Rock over 300 years, after almost all of the Spanish population left in 1704.
      </p>
      <p>
       Origin of surnames in the electoral roll by percentage is: British (27%), Spanish (26%, mostly
       <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">
        Andalusian
       </a>
       but also some 2%
       <a href="/wiki/Menorca" title="Menorca">
        Menorcan
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">
        Genoese
       </a>
       and other
       <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">
        Italian
       </a>
       (15%),
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       (15%), and
       <a href="/wiki/Maltese_people" title="Maltese people">
        Maltese
       </a>
       (8%). There are also small (less than 1%) populations of other groups such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moroccan_people" title="Moroccan people">
        Moroccans
       </a>
       , French,
       <a href="/wiki/Austrians" title="Austrians">
        Austrians
       </a>
       , Chinese, Japanese,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_people" title="Polish people">
        Polish
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danish_people" title="Danish people">
        Danish
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable sortable collapsible" style="font-size: 90%;">

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Language">
        Language
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Language">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Gibraltar" title="Languages of Gibraltar">
        Languages of Gibraltar
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">
        official language
       </a>
       of Gibraltar is English, and is used by the government and in schools. Most locals are
       <a href="/wiki/Multilingualism" title="Multilingualism">
        bilingual
       </a>
       , also speaking Spanish. However, because of the varied mix of ethnic groups which reside there, other languages are also spoken on the Rock.
       <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">
        Berber
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">
        Arabic
       </a>
       are spoken by the
       <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
        Moroccan
       </a>
       community, as are
       <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">
        Hindi
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sindhi_language" title="Sindhi language">
        Sindhi
       </a>
       by the Indian and the Pakistani communities.
       <a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">
        Maltese
       </a>
       is spoken by some families of
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Maltese_in_Gibraltar" title="History of the Maltese in Gibraltar">
        Maltese descent
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Archer2013_78-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Archer2013-78">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Gibraltarians often converse in
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Llanito" title="Llanito">
         Llanito
        </a>
       </i>
       (
       <small>
        pronounced
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">
         [ʎaˈnito]
        </a>
       </span>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-creole_79-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-creole-79">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       a
       <a href="/wiki/Vernacular" title="Vernacular">
        vernacular
       </a>
       unique to Gibraltar. It is based on
       <a href="/wiki/Andalusian_Spanish" title="Andalusian Spanish">
        Andalusian Spanish
       </a>
       with a strong mixture of
       <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">
        British English
       </a>
       and elements from languages such as Maltese,
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Genoese_dialect" title="Genoese dialect">
        Genoese Italian
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Haketia" title="Haketia">
        Haketia
       </a>
       (a
       <a href="/wiki/Judaeo-Spanish" title="Judaeo-Spanish">
        Judaeo-Spanish
       </a>
       dialect). Llanito also often involves
       <a href="/wiki/Code-switching" title="Code-switching">
        code-switching
       </a>
       to English, with technical terms and complex ideas mostly expressed in English.
      </p>
      <p>
       Gibraltarians often call themselves
       <i>
        Llanitos
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kellermann2001_80-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Kellermann2001-80">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
        Religion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">

         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
           Hindu
          </td>
          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
           <div style="background:#800080; width:2.0%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>
          </td>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
           2.0%
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
           Other/not stated
          </td>
          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
           <div style="background:#000000; width:1.3%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>
          </td>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
           1.3%
          </td>
         </tr>
        </table>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       According to the 2012 census, approximately 72.1% of Gibraltarians are Roman Catholics.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_81-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-auto-81">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The 16th century
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Saint_Mary_the_Crowned" title="Cathedral of Saint Mary the Crowned">
        Saint Mary the Crowned
       </a>
       is the cathedral church of the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Gibraltar" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Gibraltar">
        Roman Catholic Diocese of Gibraltar
       </a>
       , and also the oldest Catholic church in the territory. Other Christian denominations include the
       <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">
        Church of England
       </a>
       (7.7%), whose
       <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity,_Gibraltar" title="Cathedral of the Holy Trinity, Gibraltar">
        Cathedral of the Holy Trinity
       </a>
       is the cathedral of the Anglican
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Gibraltar_in_Europe" title="Bishop of Gibraltar in Europe">
        Bishop of Gibraltar in Europe
       </a>
       ; the
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Methodist_Church" title="Gibraltar Methodist Church">
        Gibraltar Methodist Church
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">
        Church of Scotland
       </a>
       , various
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentecostal" title="Pentecostal">
        Pentecostal
       </a>
       and independent churches mostly influenced by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/House_Church" title="House Church">
        House Church
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charismatic_movement" title="Charismatic movement">
        Charismatic movements
       </a>
       , as well as a
       <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Brethren" title="Plymouth Brethren">
        Plymouth Brethren
       </a>
       congregation. Several of these congregations are represented by the Gibraltar Evangelical Alliance.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="467" data-file-width="700" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity.jpg/220px-Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity.jpg/330px-Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity.jpg/440px-Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity,_Gibraltar" title="Cathedral of the Holy Trinity, Gibraltar">
          Cathedral of the Holy Trinity
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       There is also a
       <a href="/wiki/Ward_(LDS_Church)" title="Ward (LDS Church)">
        ward
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">
        The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints
       </a>
       , and two congregations of
       <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">
        Jehovah's Witnesses
       </a>
       . 7.1% advised that they have no religion. The Gibraltar Secular Humanist Society also holds regular meetings.
      </p>
      <p>
       The third religion in size is
       <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
        Islam
       </a>
       (3.6% of the population). There is also an established
       <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">
        Hindu
       </a>
       population (2%), members of the
       <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bahá'í Faith">
        Bahá'í Faith
       </a>
       and a long-established
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Gibraltar" title="History of the Jews in Gibraltar">
        Jewish community
       </a>
       , which, at 763 persons, accounts for 2.4% of the population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_81-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-auto-81">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As a share of the total population, this is the second-largest Jewish population in the world, trailing only
       <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
        Israel
       </a>
       . There are four functioning
       <a href="/wiki/Synagogues_of_Gibraltar" title="Synagogues of Gibraltar">
        Orthodox synagogues in Gibraltar
       </a>
       and several kosher establishments.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Gibraltar" title="Education in Gibraltar">
        Education in Gibraltar
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Arms_of_The_University_of_Gibraltar.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="182" data-file-width="170" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5e/The_Arms_of_The_University_of_Gibraltar.JPG" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Arms_of_The_University_of_Gibraltar.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Arms of The University of Gibraltar
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Gibraltar" title="Education in Gibraltar">
        Education in Gibraltar
       </a>
       generally follows the
       <a href="/wiki/Education_in_England" title="Education in England">
        English model
       </a>
       , operating within a
       <a href="/wiki/Three-tier_education" title="Three-tier education">
        three tier system
       </a>
       . Schools in Gibraltar use the
       <a href="/wiki/Key_Stage" title="Key Stage">
        Key Stage
       </a>
       modular approach to teach the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Curriculum_(England,_Wales_and_Northern_Ireland)" title="National Curriculum (England, Wales and Northern Ireland)">
        National Curriculum
       </a>
       . Gibraltar has 15
       <a href="/wiki/State_school" title="State school">
        state schools
       </a>
       , two private schools and a college of further education,
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_College" title="Gibraltar College">
        Gibraltar College
       </a>
       . Government secondary schools are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bayside_Comprehensive_School_(Gibraltar)" title="Bayside Comprehensive School (Gibraltar)">
        Bayside Comprehensive School
       </a>
       for boys and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Westside_School_(Gibraltar)" title="Westside School (Gibraltar)">
        Westside School
       </a>
       for girls, and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Prior_Park_School_Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Prior Park School Gibraltar (page does not exist)">
        Prior Park School Gibraltar
       </a>
       is an independent coeducational secondary school.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 31 March 2015 the government of Gibraltar announced the adoption of the University of Gibraltar Act and The
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Gibraltar" title="University of Gibraltar">
        University of Gibraltar
       </a>
       opened in September 2015.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
        <a href="#cite_note-85">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Previously, there were no facilities in Gibraltar for full-time higher education, and consequently, all Gibraltarian students studied elsewhere at
       <a href="/wiki/Academic_degree" title="Academic degree">
        degree
       </a>
       level or its equivalent and also for certain non-degree courses.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Government of Gibraltar operates a scholarship/grant system to provide funding for students studying in the United Kingdom. All Gibraltarian students used to follow the
       <a href="/wiki/Student_loans_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Student loans in the United Kingdom">
        UK student loans procedure
       </a>
       , applying for a loan from the
       <a href="/wiki/Student_Loans_Company" title="Student Loans Company">
        Student Loans Company
       </a>
       which was then reimbursed in full by the Government of Gibraltar. In August 2010, this system was replaced by the direct payment by the government of grants and tuition fees. The overwhelming majority of Gibraltarians continue their studies at university level.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Health_care">
        Health care
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Health care">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       All Gibraltarians are entitled to health care in public
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ward" title="wikt:ward">
        wards
       </a>
       and clinics at the St Bernard hospital and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_health_care" title="Primary health care">
        primary health care
       </a>
       centre. All other British citizens are also entitled to free-of-charge treatment on the Rock on presentation of a valid
       <a href="/wiki/British_passport" title="British passport">
        British passport
       </a>
       during stays of up to 30 days. Other EU nationals are equally entitled to treatment on presentation of a valid
       <a href="/wiki/European_Health_Insurance_Card" title="European Health Insurance Card">
        European Health Insurance Card
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Dental_surgery" title="Dental surgery">
        Dental treatment
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Prescription_drug" title="Prescription drug">
        prescribed medicines
       </a>
       are free of charge for Gibraltarian students and
       <a href="/wiki/Pensioner" title="Pensioner">
        pensioners
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Health_Authority" title="Gibraltar Health Authority">
        Gibraltar Health Authority
       </a>
       is funded through the
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Group_Practice_Medical_Scheme" title="Gibraltar Group Practice Medical Scheme">
        Gibraltar Group Practice Medical Scheme
       </a>
       . It employs around 900 people, handling 37,000
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accident_and_emergency" title="Accident and emergency">
        A&amp;E
       </a>
       attendances, 40,000 outpatient appointments, and 90,000
       <a href="/wiki/General_practitioner" title="General practitioner">
        GP
       </a>
       visits a year. Some specialist care is provided by visiting consultants and in UK and Spanish hospitals. First-line medical and nursing services are provided at the Primary Care Centre, which has 16 GPs, with more specialised services available at
       <a href="/wiki/St_Bernard%27s_Hospital" title="St Bernard's Hospital">
        St Bernard's Hospital
       </a>
       , a 210-bed civilian hospital opened in 2005. Psychiatric care is provided by
       <a href="/wiki/King_George_V_Hospital_(Gibraltar)" title="King George V Hospital (Gibraltar)">
        King George V Hospital
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Gibraltar" title="Culture of Gibraltar">
        Culture of Gibraltar
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Tercentenary_flag_display.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="465" data-file-width="300" height="341" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Gibraltar_Tercentenary_flag_display.jpg/220px-Gibraltar_Tercentenary_flag_display.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c4/Gibraltar_Tercentenary_flag_display.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Tercentenary_flag_display.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tercentenary" title="Tercentenary">
          Tercentenary
         </a>
         celebrations in Gibraltar.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Gibraltar" title="Culture of Gibraltar">
        culture of Gibraltar
       </a>
       reflects Gibraltarians' diverse origins. While there are Spanish (mostly from nearby
       <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">
        Andalusia
       </a>
       ) and British influences, the ethnic origins of most Gibraltarians are not confined to these ethnicities. Other ethnicities include
       <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">
        Genoese
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Maltese_people" title="Maltese people">
        Maltese
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">
        German
       </a>
       . A few other Gibraltar residents are
       <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">
        Jewish of Sephardic
       </a>
       origin,
       <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
        Moroccan
       </a>
       , or
       <a href="/wiki/Non-resident_Indian_and_person_of_Indian_origin" title="Non-resident Indian and person of Indian origin">
        Indians
       </a>
       . British influence remains strong, with English being the language of government, commerce, education and the media.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_sovereignty_referendum,_1967" title="Gibraltar sovereignty referendum, 1967">
        Gibraltar's first sovereignty referendum
       </a>
       is celebrated annually on
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_National_Day" title="Gibraltar National Day">
        Gibraltar National Day
       </a>
       (10 September). It is a public holiday, during which most Gibraltarians dress in their
       <a href="/wiki/National_colours" title="National colours">
        national colours
       </a>
       of red and white. Until 2016, the tradition had been to also release 30,000 similarly coloured balloons, which represented the people of Gibraltar. However, this tradition has now been ended because of the threat that it poses to wildlife, particularly marine.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The 300th anniversary of
       <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Gibraltar" title="Capture of Gibraltar">
        Gibraltar's capture
       </a>
       was celebrated in 2004 on Tercentenary Day (4 August), when in recognition of and with thanks for its long association with Gibraltar, the
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">
        Royal Navy
       </a>
       was given the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Freedom_of_the_City_of_Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Freedom of the City of Gibraltar (page does not exist)">
        Freedom of the City of Gibraltar
       </a>
       and a human chain of Gibraltarians dressed in red, white and blue, linked hands to encircle the Rock. On 4 June 2012, the
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Diamond_Jubilee_Flotilla" title="Gibraltar Diamond Jubilee Flotilla">
        Gibraltar Diamond Jubilee Flotilla
       </a>
       , inspired by the
       <a href="/wiki/Thames_Diamond_Jubilee_Pageant" title="Thames Diamond Jubilee Pageant">
        Thames Diamond Jubilee Pageant
       </a>
       , celebrated sixty years of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" title="Queen Elizabeth II">
        Queen
       </a>
       's reign.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Gibraltar Broadcasting Corporation">
        Gibraltar Broadcasting Corporation
       </a>
       operates a television and radio station on UHF, VHF and medium-wave. The radio service is also internet-streamed. Special events and the daily news bulletin are streamed in video. The other local radio service is operated by the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Forces_Broadcasting_Service" title="British Forces Broadcasting Service">
        British Forces Broadcasting Service
       </a>
       which also provides a limited cable television network to HM Forces. The largest and most frequently published newspaper is the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Chronicle" title="Gibraltar Chronicle">
         Gibraltar Chronicle
        </a>
       </i>
       , Gibraltar's oldest established daily newspaper and the world's second oldest English language newspaper to have been in print continuously
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with daily editions six days a week.
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Panorama_(Gibraltar)" title="Panorama (Gibraltar)">
         Panorama
        </a>
       </i>
       is published on weekdays, and
       <i>
        7 Days
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        The New People
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        Gibsport
       </i>
       are weekly.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_National_Day_027_(9719742224)_(2).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1310" data-file-width="1969" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Gibraltar_National_Day_027_%289719742224%29_%282%29.jpg/220px-Gibraltar_National_Day_027_%289719742224%29_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Gibraltar_National_Day_027_%289719742224%29_%282%29.jpg/330px-Gibraltar_National_Day_027_%289719742224%29_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Gibraltar_National_Day_027_%289719742224%29_%282%29.jpg/440px-Gibraltar_National_Day_027_%289719742224%29_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_National_Day_027_(9719742224)_(2).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Thousands of
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gibraltarian_people" title="Gibraltarian people">
          Gibraltarians
         </a>
         dress in their national colours of red and white during the 2013
         <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_National_Day" title="Gibraltar National Day">
          Gibraltar National Day
         </a>
         celebrations.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Native Gibraltarians have produced some literature of note. The first in fiction was probably
       <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A9ctor_Licudi" title="Héctor Licudi">
        Héctor Licudi
       </a>
       's 1929 novel
       <i>
        Barbarita
       </i>
       , written in Spanish,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       chronicling the largely autobiographical adventures of a young Gibraltarian man. Throughout the 1940s and 1950s, several anthologies of poetry were published by
       <a href="/wiki/Leopoldo_Sanguinetti" title="Leopoldo Sanguinetti">
        Leopoldo Sanguinetti
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Albert_Joseph_Patron&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Albert Joseph Patron (page does not exist)">
        Albert Joseph Patron
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Pizzarello" title="Alberto Pizzarello">
        Alberto Pizzarello
       </a>
       . The 1960s were largely dominated by the theatrical works of
       <a href="/wiki/Elio_Cruz" title="Elio Cruz">
        Elio Cruz
       </a>
       and his two highly acclaimed Spanish language plays
       <i>
        La Lola se va pá Londre
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Connie con cama camera en el comedor
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       In the 1990s, the Gibraltarian
       <a href="/wiki/Intellectual" title="Intellectual">
        man-of-letters
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Mario_Arroyo" title="Mario Arroyo">
        Mario Arroyo
       </a>
       published
       <i>
        Profiles
       </i>
       (1994), a series of bilingual meditations on love, loneliness and death.
       <a href="/wiki/Trino_Cruz" title="Trino Cruz">
        Trino Cruz
       </a>
       is a bilingual poet originally writing English but now mainly in Spanish, who also translates
       <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">
        Maghreb
       </a>
       poetry.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ElPais_93-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ElPais-93">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Téllez2013_94-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Téllez2013-94">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Of late there have been works by the essayist
       <a href="/wiki/Mary_Chiappe" title="Mary Chiappe">
        Mary Chiappe
       </a>
       , such as her volume of essays
       <i>
        Cabbages and Kings
       </i>
       (2006) and by
       <a href="/wiki/M._G._Sanchez" title="M. G. Sanchez">
        M. G. Sanchez
       </a>
       , author of the books
       <i>
        Rock Black: Ten Gibraltarian Stories
       </i>
       (2008) and
       <i>
        Diary of a Victorian Colonial
       </i>
       (2009). Mary Chiappe and
       <a href="/wiki/Sam_Benady" title="Sam Benady">
        Sam Benady
       </a>
       have also published a series of detective books centred on the character of the nineteenth-century Gibraltarian sleuth Bresciano.
      </p>
      <p>
       Musicians from Gibraltar include
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Ramirez" title="Charles Ramirez">
        Charles Ramirez
       </a>
       , the first guitarist invited to play with the
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Music" title="Royal College of Music">
        Royal College of Music
       </a>
       Orchestra,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       successful rock bands like
       <a href="/wiki/Breed_77" title="Breed 77">
        Breed 77
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Melon_Diesel" title="Melon Diesel">
        Melon Diesel
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Taxi_(Gibraltar_band)" title="Taxi (Gibraltar band)">
        Taxi
       </a>
       , while Gibraltarian bassist Glen Diani played for Irish/British
       <a href="/wiki/Nu_metal" title="Nu metal">
        nu metal
       </a>
       group
       <a href="/wiki/One_Minute_Silence" title="One Minute Silence">
        One Minute Silence
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Albert_Hammond" title="Albert Hammond">
        Albert Hammond
       </a>
       had top 10 hits in the UK and US and has written many songs for international artists such as
       <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">
        Whitney Houston
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tina_Turner" title="Tina Turner">
        Tina Turner
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Julio_Iglesias" title="Julio Iglesias">
        Julio Iglesias
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Gibraltarian cuisine is the result of a long relationship between the Andalusian Spaniards and the British, as well as the many foreigners who made Gibraltar their home over the past three centuries. The culinary influences include those from Malta, Genoa, Portugal, Andalusia and Britain. This marriage of tastes has given Gibraltar an eclectic mix of Mediterranean and British cuisine.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Profiteroles" title="Profiteroles">
        Profiteroles
       </a>
       , a French
       <a href="/wiki/Choux_pastry" title="Choux pastry">
        choux pastry
       </a>
       ball with a sweet
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filling_(cooking)" title="Filling (cooking)">
        filling
       </a>
       of whipped cream, is considered to be Gibraltar's
       <a href="/wiki/National_dish" title="National dish">
        national dish
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These are often served after a meal including
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Calentita" title="Calentita">
        Calentita
       </a>
       , a baked bread-like dish made with
       <a href="/wiki/Gram_flour" title="Gram flour">
        chickpea flour
       </a>
       , water, olive oil, salt and pepper.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">
        Sport
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Sport">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Gibraltar" title="Sport in Gibraltar">
        Sport in Gibraltar
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           needs additional citations for
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            verification
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit">
            improve this article
           </a>

          </span>
          <small>

            (July 2011)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
