            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_starting_XI.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1310" data-file-width="1969" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Gibraltar_starting_XI.jpg/220px-Gibraltar_starting_XI.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Gibraltar_starting_XI.jpg/330px-Gibraltar_starting_XI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Gibraltar_starting_XI.jpg/440px-Gibraltar_starting_XI.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_starting_XI.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_national_football_team" title="Gibraltar national football team">
          Gibraltar national football team
         </a>
         lining up in their first official match in 2013
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 2007, there were 18 Gibraltar sports associations with official recognition from their respective international
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sport_governing_body" title="Sport governing body">
        governing bodies
       </a>
       . Others have submitted applications for recognition which are being considered. The government supports the many sporting associations financially. Gibraltar also competes in the bi-annual
       <a href="/wiki/International_Island_Games_Association" title="International Island Games Association">
        Island Games
       </a>
       , which it hosted in 1995.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Gibraltar" title="Football in Gibraltar">
        Football
       </a>
       is a popular sport in Gibraltar. The
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Football_Association" title="Gibraltar Football Association">
        Gibraltar Football Association
       </a>
       applied for full membership of
       <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">
        UEFA
       </a>
       , but their bid was turned down in 2007 in a contentious decision.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Sport_98-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BBC_Sport-98">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Gibraltar was confirmed as UEFA's 54th member on 24 May 2013 as a result of
       <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Arbitration_for_Sport" title="Court of Arbitration for Sport">
        Court of Arbitration for Sport
       </a>
       (CAS) arbitration and played in
       <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">
        Euro 2016
       </a>
       qualifications.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_100-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-100">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Their first match was a 0–0 draw against Slovakia. Subsequently, Gibraltar applied for FIFA membership but this bid was also turned down.
      </p>
      <p>
       On 2 May 2016 the CAS upheld the appeal filed by the Gibraltar Football Association regarding its request to become a full-time member of FIFA. CAS ordered FIFA to stop blocking Gibraltar's application for membership and allow it "without delay".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Cricket_Association" title="Gibraltar Cricket Association">
        Cricket
       </a>
       enjoys popularity in Gibraltar. The
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_national_cricket_team" title="Gibraltar national cricket team">
        Gibraltar national cricket team
       </a>
       won the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Cricket_Championship" title="European Cricket Championship">
        European Cricket Championship
       </a>
       Division Two in 2000 and 2002.
       <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Gibraltar" title="Rugby union in Gibraltar">
        Rugby union
       </a>
       is fairly popular and one of the fastest growing team sports,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar_Rugby_Union_Football_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gibraltar Rugby Union Football Union (page does not exist)">
        Gibraltar Rugby Union Football Union
       </a>
       applied for membership of Europe's governing body for rugby. Gibraltar is believed to be the birthplace of the rugby variant
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tag_Rugby" title="Tag Rugby">
        Tag Rugby
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [nb 2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar_Rifle_Association&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gibraltar Rifle Association (page does not exist)">
        Gibraltar Rifle Association
       </a>
       (GRA) was Gibraltar's most successful team at the 2009 Island Games, earning four gold medals.
      </p>
      <p>
       Darts is also a popular sport, with the Gibraltar Darts Association (a full member of World Darts Federation since 1977) running leagues and other regular tournaments. In 2010, Gibraltar hosted and won the Mediterranean Cup, competing against France, Italy, Turkey, Malta and Cyprus.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">
        Communications
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Communications">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Telex1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="260" data-file-width="400" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Telex1.jpg/220px-Telex1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Telex1.jpg/330px-Telex1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7c/Telex1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Telex1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A plaque in City Mill Lane marking the site of Gibraltar's first telephone exchange.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Victorian_Post_Box_of_1887_in_use_at_Gibraltar_in_2008.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="848" data-file-width="512" height="282" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Victorian_Post_Box_of_1887_in_use_at_Gibraltar_in_2008.jpg/170px-Victorian_Post_Box_of_1887_in_use_at_Gibraltar_in_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Victorian_Post_Box_of_1887_in_use_at_Gibraltar_in_2008.jpg/255px-Victorian_Post_Box_of_1887_in_use_at_Gibraltar_in_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Victorian_Post_Box_of_1887_in_use_at_Gibraltar_in_2008.jpg/340px-Victorian_Post_Box_of_1887_in_use_at_Gibraltar_in_2008.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Victorian_Post_Box_of_1887_in_use_at_Gibraltar_in_2008.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A Victorian post box of standard 1887 UK design in use in Gibraltar's Main Street (2008).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_Gibraltar" title="Communications in Gibraltar">
        Communications in Gibraltar
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Gibraltar has a digital
       <a href="/wiki/Telephone_exchange" title="Telephone exchange">
        telephone exchange
       </a>
       supported by a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Optical_fibre" title="Optical fibre">
        fibre optic
       </a>
       and copper infrastructure; the telephone operator
       <a href="/wiki/Gibtelecom" title="Gibtelecom">
        Gibtelecom
       </a>
       also operates a
       <a href="/wiki/GSM" title="GSM">
        GSM
       </a>
       network. Internet connectivity is available across the fixed network. Gibraltar's top-level domain code is
       <a href="/wiki/.gi" title=".gi">
        .gi
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Direct_Dialling" title="International Direct Dialling">
        International Direct Dialling
       </a>
       (IDD) is provided, and Gibraltar was allocated the access code
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%2B350" title="+350">
        +350
       </a>
       by the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Telecommunication_Union" title="International Telecommunication Union">
        International Telecommunication Union
       </a>
       . This has been universally valid since 10 February 2007, when the
       <a href="/wiki/Telecom_dispute_between_Gibraltar_and_Spain" title="Telecom dispute between Gibraltar and Spain">
        telecom dispute
       </a>
       was resolved.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">
        Transport
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Transport">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Gibraltar" title="Transport in Gibraltar">
        Transport in Gibraltar
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Cable_Car_2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="2136" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gibraltar_Cable_Car_2.jpg/170px-Gibraltar_Cable_Car_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gibraltar_Cable_Car_2.jpg/255px-Gibraltar_Cable_Car_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gibraltar_Cable_Car_2.jpg/340px-Gibraltar_Cable_Car_2.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Cable_Car_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Cable_Car" title="Gibraltar Cable Car">
          Gibraltar Cable Car
         </a>
         runs from outside the
         <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Botanic_Gardens" title="Gibraltar Botanic Gardens">
          Gibraltar Botanic Gardens
         </a>
         to the top of the Rock.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Within Gibraltar, the main form of transport is the car.
       <a href="/wiki/Motorcycle" title="Motorcycle">
        Motorcycles
       </a>
       are also very popular and there is a good modern bus service. Unlike in the UK and other British territories, traffic
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Right-_and_left-hand_traffic" title="Right- and left-hand traffic">
        drives on the right
       </a>
       and speed limits are in km/h, as the territory shares a land border with Spain.
      </p>
      <p>
       There is a
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Cable_Car" title="Gibraltar Cable Car">
        Gibraltar Cable Car
       </a>
       that runs from ground level to the top of the Rock, with an intermediate station at
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Apes%27_Den&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Apes' Den (page does not exist)">
        Apes' Den
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Restrictions on transport introduced by Spanish dictator
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">
        Francisco Franco
       </a>
       closed the land frontier in 1969 and also prohibited any air or ferry connections. In 1982, the land border was reopened. As the result of an agreement signed in
       <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Spain" title="Córdoba, Spain">
        Córdoba
       </a>
       on 18 September 2006 between Gibraltar, the United Kingdom and Spain,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cordoba_104-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cordoba-104">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the Spanish government agreed to relax
       <a href="/wiki/Border_control" title="Border control">
        border controls
       </a>
       at the frontier that have plagued locals for decades; in return, Britain paid increased pensions to Spanish workers who lost their jobs when Franco closed the border.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pensions_105-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-pensions-105">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Telecommunication restrictions were lifted in February 2007 and air links with Spain were restored in December 2006.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-airport_106-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-airport-106">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The border control is the only road border control between two EU members that is expected to remain indefinitely (Bulgaria, Croatia and Romania have border controls which are expected to
       <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area#Prospective_members" title="Schengen Area">
        be removed around 2020
       </a>
       ), however Britain plans to leave the EU. Motorists and pedestrians crossing the border with Spain are occasionally subjected to very long delays.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
        <a href="#cite_note-108">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Spain has occasionally closed the border during disputes or incidents involving the Gibraltar authorities, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/MV_Aurora_(2000)#Norovirus_breakout" title="MV Aurora (2000)">
        <i>
         Aurora
        </i>
        cruise ship incident
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
        <a href="#cite_note-109">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and when fishermen from the Spanish fishing vessel
       <i>
        Piraña
       </i>
       were arrested for illegal fishing in Gibraltar waters.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
        <a href="#cite_note-110">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Air">
        Air
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Air">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_International_Airport" title="Gibraltar International Airport">
        Gibraltar International Airport
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       As of 2017, Gibraltar maintains regular flight connections with London,
       <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">
        Manchester
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">
        Bristol
       </a>
       in the UK, and with
       <a href="/wiki/Casablanca" title="Casablanca">
        Casablanca
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tangier" title="Tangier">
        Tangier
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
        Morocco
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
        <a href="#cite_note-111">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/GB_Airways" title="GB Airways">
        GB Airways
       </a>
       operated a service between Gibraltar and London and other cities for many years. The airline initially flew under the name "Gibraltar Airways". In 1989, and in anticipation of service to cities outside the UK, Gibraltar Airways changed its name to GB Airways with the belief that a new name would incur fewer political problems. As a franchise, the airline operated flights in full
       <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">
        British Airways
       </a>
       livery. In 2007, GB Airways was purchased by
       <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">
        easyJet
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
        <a href="#cite_note-112">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which began operating flights under their name in April 2008 when British Airways re-introduced flights to Gibraltar under their name. EasyJet have since added
       <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Airport" title="Bristol Airport">
        Bristol
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">
        Manchester
       </a>
       and also operated flights to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liverpool_Airport" title="Liverpool Airport">
        Liverpool
       </a>
       between 2011 and 2012. Until entering administration in October 2017,
       <a href="/wiki/Monarch_Airlines" title="Monarch Airlines">
        Monarch Airlines
       </a>
       operated the largest number of flights between the United Kingdom and Gibraltar, with scheduled services between Gibraltar and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_Luton_Airport" title="London Luton Airport">
        Luton
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">
        London Gatwick
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Airport" title="Birmingham Airport">
        Birmingham
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">
        Manchester
       </a>
       . The Spanish
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_airline" title="National airline">
        national airline
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iberia_Airlines" title="Iberia Airlines">
        Iberia
       </a>
       , operated a daily service to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barajas_Airport" title="Barajas Airport">
        Madrid
       </a>
       which ceased for lack of demand. In May 2009,
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%81ndalus_L%C3%ADneas_A%C3%A9reas" title="Ándalus Líneas Aéreas">
        Ándalus Líneas Aéreas
       </a>
       opened a Spanish service,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
        <a href="#cite_note-113">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which also ceased operations in March 2010.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
        <a href="#cite_note-114">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
       An annual return
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charter_flight" title="Charter flight">
        charter flight
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Malta_International_Airport" title="Malta International Airport">
        Malta
       </a>
       is operated by
       <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">
        Maltese
       </a>
       national airline,
       <a href="/wiki/Air_Malta" title="Air Malta">
        Air Malta
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Airport_Main_Highway.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2211" data-file-width="3888" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Gibraltar_Airport_Main_Highway.jpg/220px-Gibraltar_Airport_Main_Highway.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Gibraltar_Airport_Main_Highway.jpg/330px-Gibraltar_Airport_Main_Highway.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Gibraltar_Airport_Main_Highway.jpg/440px-Gibraltar_Airport_Main_Highway.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Airport_Main_Highway.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The main road that crosses Gibraltar Airport.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Airport_New_Terminal.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Gibraltar_Airport_New_Terminal.jpg/220px-Gibraltar_Airport_New_Terminal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Gibraltar_Airport_New_Terminal.jpg/330px-Gibraltar_Airport_New_Terminal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Gibraltar_Airport_New_Terminal.jpg/440px-Gibraltar_Airport_New_Terminal.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Airport_New_Terminal.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The new terminal at Gibraltar Airport.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Airport" title="Gibraltar Airport">
        Gibraltar International Airport
       </a>
       is unusual not only because of its proximity to the city centre resulting in the airport terminal being within walking distance of much of Gibraltar but also because the runway intersects
       <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill_Avenue" title="Winston Churchill Avenue">
        Winston Churchill Avenue
       </a>
       , the main north-south street, requiring movable barricades to close when aircraft land or depart. New roads and a tunnel, which will end the need to stop road traffic when aircraft use the runway, were planned to coincide with the building of a new
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Airport#New_terminal" title="Gibraltar Airport">
        airport terminal building
       </a>
       with an originally estimated completion date of 2009,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pressnote_115-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-pressnote-115">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
        <a href="#cite_note-116">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
       although it has not been completed because of delays.
      </p>
      <p>
       The most popular alternative airport for Gibraltar is
       <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga_Airport" title="Málaga Airport">
        Málaga Airport
       </a>
       in Spain, some 120 kilometres (75 mi) to the east, which offers a wide range of destinations, second to
       <a href="/wiki/Jerez_Airport" title="Jerez Airport">
        Jerez Airport
       </a>
       which is closer to Gibraltar. In addition, the
       <a href="/wiki/Algeciras_Heliport" title="Algeciras Heliport">
        Algeciras Heliport
       </a>
       across the bay offers scheduled services to
       <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">
        Ceuta
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sea">
        Sea
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Sea">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Cruise_Terminal" title="Gibraltar Cruise Terminal">
        Gibraltar Cruise Terminal
       </a>
       receives a large number of visits from
       <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">
        cruise ships
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">
        Strait of Gibraltar
       </a>
       is one of the busiest shipping lanes in the world.
      </p>
      <p>
       Passenger and cargo ships anchor in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Harbour" title="Gibraltar Harbour">
        Gibraltar Harbour
       </a>
       . Also, a ferry links Gibraltar with
       <a href="/wiki/Tangier" title="Tangier">
        Tangier
       </a>
       in Morocco. The ferry between Gibraltar and
       <a href="/wiki/Algeciras" title="Algeciras">
        Algeciras
       </a>
       , which had been halted in 1969 when Franco severed communications with Gibraltar, was finally reopened on 16 December 2009, served by the Spanish company
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Transcoma&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Transcoma (page does not exist)">
        Transcoma
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
        <a href="#cite_note-117">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Ferries by FRS running twice a week from Gibraltar to
       <a href="/wiki/Tanger-Med" title="Tanger-Med">
        Tanger-Med
       </a>
       port provide access to the
       <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Morocco" title="Rail transport in Morocco">
        Moroccan railway
       </a>
       system.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
        <a href="#cite_note-118">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
        <a href="#cite_note-119">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">
        Rail
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Rail">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       While railway track extends to the outskirts of
       <a href="/wiki/La_L%C3%ADnea_de_la_Concepci%C3%B3n" title="La Línea de la Concepción">
        La Línea
       </a>
       from an
       <a href="/wiki/San_Roque-La_L%C3%ADnea_railway" title="San Roque-La Línea railway">
        aborted rail expansion project in the 1970s
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
        <a href="#cite_note-120">
         [118]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
        <a href="#cite_note-121">
         [119]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the closest railway station in Spain is
       <a href="/wiki/San_Roque_station" title="San Roque station">
        San Roque station
       </a>
       , accessible via buses from
       <a href="/wiki/La_L%C3%ADnea_de_la_Concepci%C3%B3n" title="La Línea de la Concepción">
        La Línea
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">
        Water supply and sanitation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Water supply and sanitation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Gibraltar" title="Water supply and sanitation in Gibraltar">
        Water supply and sanitation in Gibraltar
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">
        Water supply
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">
        sanitation
       </a>
       in Gibraltar have been major concerns for its inhabitants throughout its history. There are no rivers, streams, or large bodies of water on the peninsula. Gibraltar's water supply was formerly provided by a combination of an aqueduct, wells, and the use of cisterns, barrels and earthenware pots to capture rainwater. This became increasingly inadequate as Gibraltar's population grew in the 18th and 19th centuries and lethal diseases such as
       <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">
        cholera
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">
        yellow fever
       </a>
       began to spread. In the late 19th century, a Sanitary Commission instigated major improvements which saw the introduction of large-scale desalination and the use of giant water catchments covering over 2.5 million square feet (nearly 250,000 m
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ). Today Gibraltar's supply of drinking water comes entirely from
       <a href="/wiki/Desalination" title="Desalination">
        desalination
       </a>
       , with a separate supply of saltwater for sanitary purposes. Both supplies are delivered from huge underground reservoirs excavated under the
       <a href="/wiki/Rock_of_Gibraltar" title="Rock of Gibraltar">
        Rock of Gibraltar
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Police">
        Police
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Police">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Gibraltar_Police" title="Royal Gibraltar Police">
        Royal Gibraltar Police
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Defence_Police" title="Gibraltar Defence Police">
        Gibraltar Defence Police
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RGP_Patrol_Car.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1156" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/RGP_Patrol_Car.JPG/220px-RGP_Patrol_Car.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/RGP_Patrol_Car.JPG/330px-RGP_Patrol_Car.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/RGP_Patrol_Car.JPG/440px-RGP_Patrol_Car.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RGP_Patrol_Car.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Royal Gibraltar Police car, 2012
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:K20P1600.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3104" data-file-width="4672" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/K20P1600.JPG/220px-K20P1600.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/K20P1600.JPG/330px-K20P1600.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/K20P1600.JPG/440px-K20P1600.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:K20P1600.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Royal_Gibraltar_Police" title="Royal Gibraltar Police">
          Royal Gibraltar Police
         </a>
         , Marine Section
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Gibraltar_Police" title="Royal Gibraltar Police">
        Royal Gibraltar Police
       </a>
       (RGP) and Gibraltar Customs are Gibraltar's principal civilian
       <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_agency" title="Law enforcement agency">
        law enforcement agencies
       </a>
       . Outside the United Kingdom, the RGP is the oldest police force of the former British Empire, formed shortly after the creation of London's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Police" title="Metropolitan Police">
        Metropolitan Police
       </a>
       in 1829 when Gibraltar was declared a
       <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">
        crown colony
       </a>
       on 25 June 1830.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
        <a href="#cite_note-122">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In general, the Gibraltar force follows British police models in its dress and its mostly male constables and sergeants on foot patrol wear the traditional
       <a href="/wiki/Custodian_helmet" title="Custodian helmet">
        custodian helmet
       </a>
       , the headgear of the British "bobby on the beat". The helmet is traditionally made of cork covered outside by felt or
       <a href="/wiki/Serge_(fabric)" title="Serge (fabric)">
        serge
       </a>
       -like material that matches the tunic. The vehicles also appear virtually identical to typical UK police vehicles, but are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Left_hand_drive" title="Left hand drive">
        left hand drive
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The force, whose name received the prefix "Royal" in 1992, currently numbers over 220 officers divided into a number of units. These include the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Criminal_Investigation_Department" title="Criminal Investigation Department">
        CID
       </a>
       , drug squad,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_branch" title="Special branch">
        special branch
       </a>
       , firearms,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scenes_of_Crime_Officer" title="Scenes of Crime Officer">
        scene of crime examiners
       </a>
       , traffic, marine and operations units, sections or departments.
      </p>
      <p>
       On 24 September 2015, the Freedom of the City of Gibraltar was conferred upon the RGP by His Worship the Mayor Adolfo Canepa.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Armed_forces">
        Armed forces
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Armed forces">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Gibraltar's defence is the responsibility of the United Kingdom tri-services
       <a href="/wiki/British_Forces_Gibraltar" title="British Forces Gibraltar">
        British Forces Gibraltar
       </a>
       . In January 2007, the Ministry of Defence announced that the private company
       <a href="/wiki/Serco" title="Serco">
        Serco
       </a>
       would provide services to the base. The announcement resulted in the affected trade unions striking.
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Royal_Gibraltar_Regiment" title="Royal Gibraltar Regiment">
         Royal Gibraltar Regiment
        </a>
        provides the army garrison with a detachment of the
        <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">
         British Army
        </a>
        , based at
        <i>
         Devils Tower Camp
        </i>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
         <a href="#cite_note-123">
          [121]
         </a>
        </sup>
        The regiment was originally a part-time reserve force until the British Army placed it on a permanent footing in 1990. The regiment includes full-time and part-time soldiers recruited from Gibraltar as well as British Army regulars posted from other regiments.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">
         Royal Navy
        </a>
        maintains a
        <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Squadron" title="Gibraltar Squadron">
         squadron
        </a>
        at the Rock. The squadron is responsible for the security and integrity of British Gibraltar Territorial Waters (BGTW). The shore establishment at Gibraltar is called
        <a href="/wiki/HMS_Rooke" title="HMS Rooke">
         HMS
         <i>
          Rooke
         </i>
        </a>
        after
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_George_Rooke" title="Sir George Rooke">
         Sir George Rooke
        </a>
        , who captured the Rock for
        <a href="/wiki/Charles_VI,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles VI, Holy Roman Emperor">
         Archduke Charles
        </a>
        (pretender to the Spanish throne) in 1704. The naval air base was named HMS
        <i>
         Cormorant.
        </i>
        Gibraltar's strategic position provides an important facility for the Royal Navy and Britain's allies. British and US nuclear submarines frequently visit the
        <i>
         Z berths
        </i>
        at Gibraltar.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
         <a href="#cite_note-124">
          [122]
         </a>
        </sup>
        A
        <a href="/wiki/Berth_(moorings)" title="Berth (moorings)">
         Z berth
        </a>
        provides the facility for nuclear submarines to visit for operational or recreational purposes and for non-nuclear repairs. During the
        <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">
         Falklands War
        </a>
        , an Argentine plan to attack British shipping in the harbour using frogmen (
        <a href="/wiki/Operation_Algeciras" title="Operation Algeciras">
         Operation Algeciras
        </a>
        ) was foiled.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
         <a href="#cite_note-125">
          [123]
         </a>
        </sup>
        The naval base also played a part in supporting the task force sent by Britain to recover the Falklands.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">
         Royal Air Force
        </a>
        station at Gibraltar forms part of Headquarters British Forces Gibraltar. Although aircraft are no longer permanently stationed at
        <a href="/wiki/RAF_Gibraltar" title="RAF Gibraltar">
         RAF Gibraltar
        </a>
        , a variety of RAF aircraft make regular visits and the airfield also houses a section from the
        <a href="/wiki/Met_Office" title="Met Office">
         Met Office
        </a>
        .
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Gibraltar has an important role in
       <a href="/wiki/Signals_intelligence" title="Signals intelligence">
        UKSIGINT
       </a>
       and provides a vital strategic part of the United Kingdom communications gathering and monitoring network in the Mediterranean and North Africa.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
        <a href="#cite_note-126">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
        <a href="#cite_note-127">
         [125]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 185px">
        <div style="width: 185px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 180px;">
          <div style="margin:15px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Merlin_Mk3s_prove_their_mettle_in_day-long_Gibraltar_transit_MOD_45160593.jpg">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="2400" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Merlin_Mk3s_prove_their_mettle_in_day-long_Gibraltar_transit_MOD_45160593.jpg/120px-Merlin_Mk3s_prove_their_mettle_in_day-long_Gibraltar_transit_MOD_45160593.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Merlin_Mk3s_prove_their_mettle_in_day-long_Gibraltar_transit_MOD_45160593.jpg/180px-Merlin_Mk3s_prove_their_mettle_in_day-long_Gibraltar_transit_MOD_45160593.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Merlin_Mk3s_prove_their_mettle_in_day-long_Gibraltar_transit_MOD_45160593.jpg/240px-Merlin_Mk3s_prove_their_mettle_in_day-long_Gibraltar_transit_MOD_45160593.jpg 2x" width="120"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           <a href="/wiki/AgustaWestland_AW101#Royal_Navy" title="AgustaWestland AW101">
            Merlin HC3
           </a>
           of
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/846_NAS" title="846 NAS">
            846 NAS
           </a>
           with
           <a href="/wiki/HMS_Scimitar_(P284)" title="HMS Scimitar (P284)">
            HMS
            <i>
             Scimitar
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 185px">
        <div style="width: 185px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 180px;">
          <div style="margin:33.5px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_navy.jpg">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="1971" data-file-width="2628" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Gibraltar_navy.jpg/150px-Gibraltar_navy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Gibraltar_navy.jpg/225px-Gibraltar_navy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Gibraltar_navy.jpg/300px-Gibraltar_navy.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           The
           <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">
            Royal Navy
           </a>
           's base in Gibraltar.
          </p>

          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           Despite several sites reporting that tag rugby was invented by Perry Haddock in Australia around 1990 (this is OzTag, a variant of Tag Rugby), Godwin's wrote about the topic seven years prior. Godwin does not mention when the sport began on Gibraltar, but he does explicitly use the term "Tag Rugby" to describe the game.

         <li id="cite_note-10">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-10">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <cite class="citation web">
            Statistics Office (2009).
            <a class="external text" href="http://www.gibraltar.gov.gi/images/stories/PDF/statistics/2009/Abstract%20of%20Statistics%20Report%202009%20Website.pdf" rel="nofollow">
             "Abstract of Statistics 2009"
            </a>
            <span style="font-size:85%;">
             (PDF)
            </span>
            . Statistics Office of the Government of Gibraltar. p. 2.
           </cite>
           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Abstract+of+Statistics+2009&amp;rft.pages=2&amp;rft.pub=Statistics+Office+of+the+Government+of+Gibraltar&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.au=Statistics+Office&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.gibraltar.gov.gi%2Fimages%2Fstories%2FPDF%2Fstatistics%2F2009%2FAbstract%2520of%2520Statistics%2520Report%25202009%2520Website.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGibraltar">
            <span style="display:none;">
            </span>
           </span>
           <i>
            The civilian population includes Gibraltarian residents, other British residents (including the wives and families of UK-based servicemen, but not the servicemen themselves) and non-British residents. Visitors and transients are not included.
           </i>
           <br/>
           In 2009, this broke down into 23,907 native-born citizens, 3,129 UK British citizens and 2,395 others, making a total population of 29,431. On census night, there were 31,623 people present in Gibraltar.
          </span>
         </li>

         <li id="cite_note-29">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-29">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <a class="external text" href="https://publications.parliament.uk/pa/cm200708/cmselect/cmfaff/c147-v/c14702.htm" rel="nofollow">
            Corrected transcript of evidence taken before the Foreign Affairs Select Committee
           </a>
           ; 28 March 2008; Answer to Question 257 by
           <a href="/wiki/Jim_Murphy" title="Jim Murphy">
            Jim Murphy
           </a>
           :
           <i>
            [T]he UK Government will never – "never" is a seldom-used word in politics – enter into an agreement on sovereignty without the agreement of the Government of Gibraltar and their people. In fact, we will never even enter into a process without that agreement.
           </i>
           <cite class="citation web">
            <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160303183041/http://www.publications.parliament.uk/pa/cm200708/cmselect/cmfaff/c147-v/c14702.htm" rel="nofollow">

               <div>
                <ul>
                 <li>
                  <span style="position: relative; top: 0.2em;">
                   <sup>
                    1
                   </sup>

                  <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">

                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <span style="position: relative; top: 0.2em;">
                   <sup>
                    2
                   </sup>
                  </span>
                  Also the seat of the
                  <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
                   European Union
                  </a>
                  , see
                  <a href="/wiki/Institutional_seats_of_the_European_Union" title="Institutional seats of the European Union">
                   Institutional seats of the European Union
                  </a>
                  and
                  <a href="/wiki/Brussels_and_the_European_Union" title="Brussels and the European Union">
                   Brussels and the European Union
                  </a>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <span style="position: relative; top: 0.2em;">
                   <sup>
                    3
                   </sup>
                  </span>
                  <a href="/wiki/List_of_transcontinental_countries" title="List of transcontinental countries">
                   Transcontinental country
                  </a>
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <span style="position: relative; top: 0.2em;">
                   <sup>
                    4
                   </sup>
                  </span>
                  Entirely in Southwest Asia but having socio-political connections with Europe
                 </li>
                 <li>
                  <span style="position: relative; top: 0.2em;">
                   <sup>
                    5
                   </sup>
                  </span>
                  <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition" title="List of states with limited recognition">
                   Partially recognised country
                  </a>
                 </li>
                </ul>
               </div>
              </td>
             </tr>
            </table>
           </div>

                     </a>
                     with the United States.
                    </li>
                    <li>
                     2. In 1931, Canada and other British
                     <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">
                      dominions
                     </a>
                     obtained self-government through the
                     <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">
                      Statute of Westminster
                     </a>
                     . See
                     <a href="/wiki/Name_of_Canada" title="Name of Canada">
                      Name of Canada
                     </a>
                     .
                    </li>
                    <li>
                     3. Gave up
                     <a href="/wiki/Responsible_government" title="Responsible government">
                      self-rule
                     </a>
                     in 1934, but remained a
                     <i>
                      <a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">
                       de jure
                      </a>
                     </i>
                     Dominion until it
                     <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">
                      joined Canada
                     </a>
                     in 1949.
                    </li>
